```R
sfiles = getGEOSuppFiles('GSE107637')
```


```R
fnames = rownames(sfiles)
ca_exp = read.delim(fnames[1],header=TRUE,check.names = FALSE)
```


```R
read.table(fnames[1],header=TRUE,check.names=FALSE,nrows = 1)[1,1:13]
```

```R
samples <- data.frame(lapply(colnames(ca_exp)[2:13],
FUN=function(x){unlist(strsplit(x, split = "\\_"))[c(1,2)]}))
```


```R
colnames(samples)<- colnames(ca_exp)[2:13]
```


```R
rownames(samples) <- c("cell_type", "inhibition")
```


```R
samples <- data.frame(t(samples))
samples
```

```R
#translate out counts into counts per million using the edgeR package function cpm
cpms = cpm(ca_exp[,2:13])
```


```R
# get rid of low counts
rownames(cpms) <- ca_exp[,1]
```


```R
cpms
```

```R
#Distribution of our data - Boxplot
data2plot <- log2(cpm(ca_exp_filtered[,2:13]))
```


```R
boxplot(data2plot, xlab = "Samples", ylab = "log2 CPM",
las = 2, cex = 0.5, cex.lab = 0.5,
cex.axis = 0.5, main = "DNASeq Samples")
#draw the median on each box plot
abline(h = median(apply(data2plot, 2, median)), col = "green", lwd = 0.6, lty = "dashed")
counts_density <- apply(log2(cpm(ca_exp_filtered[,2:13])), 2, density)
```

```R
#calculate the limits across all the samples
xlim <- 0; ylim <- 0
for (i in 1:length(counts_density)) {
xlim <- range(c(xlim, counts_density[[i]]$x));
ylim <- range(c(ylim, counts_density[[i]]$y))
}
cols <- rainbow(length(counts_density))
ltys <- rep(1, length(counts_density))
#plot the first density plot to initialize the plot
plot(counts_density[[1]], xlim=xlim, ylim=ylim, type="n",
ylab="Smoothing density of log2-CPM", main="", cex.lab = 0.85)
#plot each line
for (i in 1:length(counts_density)) lines(counts_density[[i]], col=cols[i], lty=ltys[i])
#create legend
legend("topright", colnames(data2plot),
col=cols, lty=ltys, cex=0.75,
border ="blue",  text.col = "green4",
merge = TRUE, bg = "gray90")
```

```R
#get the normalized data
normalized_counts <- cpm(d)
```


```R
#plot the normalized data
data2plot <- log2(normalized_counts)
boxplot(data2plot, xlab = "Samples", ylab = "log2 CPM",
las = 2, cex = 0.5, cex.lab = 0.5,
cex.axis = 0.5, main = "Normalized DNASeq Samples")
abline(h = median(apply(data2plot, 2, median)), col = "green", lwd = 0.6, lty = "dashed")
counts_density <- apply(log2(normalized_counts), 2, density)
```

```R
# find the outliers
outliers <- boxplot(data2plot, plot=FALSE)$out
outliers = data2plot[data2plot == -Inf]
length(outliers)
```

```R
counts_density <- apply(log2(normalized_counts), 2, density)
xlim <- 0; ylim <- 0
for (i in 1:length(counts_density)) {
xlim <- range(c(xlim, counts_density[[i]]$x));
ylim <- range(c(ylim, counts_density[[i]]$y))
}
cols <- rainbow(length(counts_density))
ltys <- rep(1, length(counts_density))
#plot the first density plot to initialize the plot
plot(counts_density[[1]], xlim=xlim, ylim=ylim, type="n",
ylab="Normalized Smoothing density of log2-CPM", main="", cex.lab = 0.85)
#plot each line
for (i in 1:length(counts_density)) lines(counts_density[[i]], col=cols[i], lty=ltys[i])
#create legend
legend("topright", colnames(data2plot),
col=cols, lty=ltys, cex=0.75,
border ="blue",  text.col = "green4",
merge = TRUE, bg = "gray90")
```

```R
# A MDS plot represents the distances between samples
plotMDS(d, labels=rownames(samples),
  col = c("darkgreen","blue")[factor(samples$cell_type)])
```

```R
#estimate common and tagwise dispersion
model_design <- model.matrix(~samples$cell_type + samples$inhibition+0)
d <- estimateDisp(d, model_design)
d
```

```R
# HGNC symbols to Human Ensembl Gene Ids
conversion_stash <- "ca_id_add_conversion.rds"
if(file.exists(conversion_stash)){
ca_id_add_conversion <- readRDS(conversion_stash)
} else {
ca_id_add_conversion <- getBM(attributes = c("hgnc_symbol","ensembl_gene_id"),
filters = c("hgnc_symbol"),
values = ca_exp_filtered$Gene,
mart = ensembl)
saveRDS(ca_id_add_conversion, conversion_stash)
}
```


```R
nrow(normalized_counts) - nrow(ca_id_add_conversion)
```

```R
## what are the control and test conditions of the dataset?
Ans: H2009 unt samples and H569 unt samples.
```


```R
## Why is the dataset of interest to you?
Ans: This data is interesting to me because this experiment is about analyzing the transcriptomic response 
of RUVBL1 knockdown (siBL1) or RUVBL1 inhibition (compB) in two different non-small cell lung cancer 
cell lines (H2009 and H596). And each group has two duplications and set the untreated samples as 
the the test conditions. So I believe learning about the role of RUVBL1/2 will be an interesting study.
```


```R
## Were there expression values that were not unique for specific genes? How did you handle these?
Ans: There is no replicate for any specific genes. Get the summarized counts for each gene and find the output which is greater than 1. If there is any, 
then it is a replicate and we remove it from the dataset.
```


```R
## Were there expression values that could not be mapped to current HUGO symbols?
Ans: Yes, there are 1126. In this samples, we mapped hgnc_symbol to ensembl_gene_id.
```


```R
## How many outliers were removed?
Ans: 2573 outliers were removed from the boxplot.
```


```R
## How did you handle replicate?
Ans: Get the summarized counts for each gene and find the output which is greater than 1. If there is any, 
then it is a replicate and we remove it from the dataset.
```

```R
## what is the final coverage of the dataset?
Ans: The total original dataset size is 13481.
     After filter, its size is 13336.
     Remove the 2573 outliers, the size is 10763.
     Remove 1126 samples who has no ensembl_gene_id, the final size is 9637.
```
